
================================================================================
Task 12/183: Two pipes can fill a pool together in 4 hours. The first pipe alone takes 6 hours longer than the second pipe alone. How long would each pipe take individually?
Category: Mathematics & Quantitative Reasoning | Type: word-problems | Difficulty: difficult
================================================================================

│ Two pipes can fill a pool together in 4 hours. The first pipe alone takes 6 hours longer than the second pipe alone. How long would each   │
│ pipe take individually?                                                                                                                    │

Output message of the LLM: ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
                                                                                                                                              
                                                                                                                                              
You will answer questions on these two pipes in four parts.                                                                                   
                                                                                                                                              
<b>PART ONE - BOTH PIPES AT FULL SPEED</b>                                                                                                    
                                                                                                                                              
The first pipe alone takes 6 hours longer than the second one. That means that the second pipe alone is slower by 3 hours. The first one alone
is faster by 4 hours, and together they are equal. Therefore each of them would take 10 hours to fill a pool completely.                      
                                                                                                                                              
<b>PART TWO - ONE PIPE AT FULL SPEED AND THE OTHER IS HALF-FULL</b>                                                                           
                                                                                                                                              
The first pipe alone takes 6 hours longer than the second one. That means that the second pipe alone is slower by 3 hours. The first one alone
is faster by 4 hours, and together they are equal. Therefore each of them would take 10 hours to fill a pool completely.                      
                                                                                                                                              
<b>PART THREE - BOTH PIPE AT HALF-FULL SPEED</b>                                                                                              
                                                                                                                                              
The first pipe alone takes 6 hours longer than the second one. That means that the second pipe alone is slower by 3 hours. The first one alone
is faster by 4 hours, and together they are equal. Therefore each of them would take 10 hours to fill a pool completely.

strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?

1. A man is in a boat. He has two sails. The first one is twice as long, but only half as high as the second one. He can row by using 4 times 
the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?                                                               
                                                                                                                                              
2. A man is in a boat. He has two sails. The first one is twice as long, but only half as high as the second one. He can row by using 4 times 
the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?

the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?                                                               
                                                                                                                                              
The first pipe alone takes 6 hours longer than the second one. That means that the second pipe alone is slower by 3 hours. The first one alone
is faster by 4 hours, and together they are equal. Therefore each of them would take 10 hours to fill a pool completely.

SOLUTION: A man is in a boat. He has two sails. The first one is twice as long, but only half as high as the second one. He can row by using 4
times the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?

as the second one. He can row by using 4 times the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?

If you like this task please share it with your friends!

1. A man is in a boat. He has two sails. The first one is twice as long, but only half as high as the second one. He can row by using 4 times 
the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?

2. A man is in a boat. He has two sails. The first one is twice as long, but only half as high as the second one. He can row by using 4 times 
the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?

SOLUTION:

1. A man is in a boat. He has two sails. The first one is twice as long, but only half as high as the second one. He can row by using 4 times 
the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?

The first pipe alone takes 6 hours longer than the second one. That means that the second pipe alone is slower by 3 hours. The first one alone
is faster by 4 hours, and together they are equal. Therefore each of them would take 10 hours to fill a pool completely.

2. A man is in a boat. He has two sails. The first one is twice as long, but only half as high as the second one. He can row by using 4 times 
the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?

The first pipe alone takes 6 hours longer than the second one. That means that the second pipe alone is slower by 3 hours. The first one alone
is faster by 4 hours, and together they are equal. Therefore each of them would take 10 hours to fill a pool completely.

2. A man is in a boat. He has two sails. The first one is twice as long, but only half as high as the second one. He can row by using 4 times 
the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?

The first pipe alone takes 6 hours longer than the second one. That means that the second pipe alone is slower by 3 hours. The first one alone
is faster by 4 hours, and together they are equal. Therefore each of them would take 10 hours to fill a pool completely.

the strength of the first sail. What is the minimum strength of the first sail?
